[1mูุคููุงุช ุฏููุงุฑุช [0m

The two-volume selection by Cottingham, Stoothoff, and Murdoch (see under Texts and Translations) is the most satisfactory 
collection of Descartesโs writings in English. Individual philosophical texts by Descartes are also widely available in paperback 
editions published by Penguin, Everyman, Mentor, and Nelson. A particularly useful translation by Stephen Voss of [3mThe Passions of 
the Soul [0m(Indianapolis, 1989) can also be mentioned in this connection. The selection of Descartesโs enormous correspondence 
translated by Anthony Kenny (see under Texts and Translations, p. ix) has now been corrected, enlarged, and incorporated as a 
third volume into the Cottingham, Stoothoff, and Murdoch edition of Descartesโs writings. Further correspondence, on psychology 
and ethics, has been translated by John Blom (see below). Also of interest is Descartesโs [3mConversation with Burman [0m, edited and 
translated by John Cottingham (Oxford: Clarendon Press, 1976). 

Descartesโs scientific writings are usually excerpted rather than printed complete. The selections given in Cottingharn [3met al [0m. 
should meet the needs of the general reader. For the [3mDiscourse and Essays [0min its entirety, see the English translation by Paul 
Olscamp (Indianapolis: Bobbs-Merrill, 1965). See also T. S. Hall (trans.), [3mTreatise of Man [0m(Cambridge, Mass.: Harvard University 
Press, 1972), and the translation of [3mThe Principles of Philosophy [0mpublished by Reidel in 1984. 

In French, besides the Adam and Tannery, there is an edition of Descartesโs writings by Alquiรฉ (Paris: Gamier, 1963โ73). 

[1mุงูุณูุฑุฉ ุงูุฐุงุชูุฉ [0m

The first biography of Descartes was Adrien Bailletโs [3mLa Vie de Monsieur Descartes [0m, published in 1691 (Paris: La Table Ronde, 
1946), recently reprinted by Slatkine Reprints (Geneva, 1970). Modern accounts of Descartesโs life, which at times correct 
Baillet, include Charles Adam, [3mVie et ลuvres de Descartes [0m(1910; AT, vol. 12), on which I have relied heavily, and, in English, 
Jack Vrooman, [3mRenรฉ Descartes: A Biography [0m(New York: Putnam, 1970). Much more recent is Stephen Gaukroger, [3mDescartes: An 
Intellectual Biography [0m(Oxford: Clarendon Press, 1995), which has a very full treatment of Descartesโs scientific writings. 

[1mุงููุธุฑูุฉ ุงูุนูููุฉ ูุฏููุงุฑุช [0m

Apart from Gaukrogerโs biography of Descartes, one of the few recent books to cover Descartesโs philosophy and science is Daniel 
Garberโs excellent [3mDescartesโ Metaphysical Physics [0m(Chicago: University of Chicago Press, 1992). Considerably older but still 
worth consulting is Jonathan Rรฉe, [3mDescartes [0m(London: Allen Lane, 1974). More on Descartesโs philosophy and science can be found in 
Desmond Clarke, [3mDescartesโ Philosophy of Science [0m(Manchester: Manchester University Press, 1982), and the collection of papers 
edited by Stephen Gaukroger, [3mDescartes: Philosophy, Mathematics, and Physics [0m(Brighton: Harvester, 1980). 

Descartesโs science is considered in some depth in J. F. Scott, [3mThe Scientific Work of Renรฉ Descartes [0m(London: Taylor and Francis, 
1952). Also useful is the chapter on Descartes in volume 7 of Lynn Thorndike, [3mHistory of Magic and Experimental Science [0m(New York: 
Columbia University Press, 1958). 

For a more general survey, see Gerd Buchdahl, [3mMetaphysics and the Philosophy of Science: The Classical OriginsโDescartes to Kant [0m
(Oxford: Blackwell, 1969). 

[1mููุณูุฉ ุฏููุงุฑุช [0m

Among the many good books on Descartesโs philosophy, I mention: Anthony Kenny, [3mDescartes: A Study of his Philosophy [0m(New York: 
Random House, 1968); Harry Frankfurt, [3mDemons, Dreamers and Madmen: The Defence of Reason in Descartesโs Metaphysics [0m(Indianapolis: 
Bobbs-Merrill, 1970); Bernard Williams, [3mDescartes: The Project of Pure Enquiry [0m(Harmondsworth: Penguin, 1978); E. M. Curley, [3m
Descartes against the Sceptics [0m(Oxford: Blackwell, 1978); Margaret Wilson, [3mDescartes [0m(London: Routledge and Kegan Paul, 1978); 
John Cottingham, [3mDescartes [0m(Oxford: Blackwell, 1986). 

Recent collections of articles on Descartesโs philosophy include John Cottingham (ed.), [3mThe Cambridge Companion to Descartes [0m
(Cambridge: Cambridge University Press, 1992), Stephen Voss, [3mEssays on the Philosophy and Science of Descartes [0m(Oxford: Oxford 
University Press, 1993), and John Cottingham (ed.), [3mReason, Will and Sensation: Essays on Descartesโs Metaphysics [0m(Oxford: 
Clarendon Press, 1994). A collection of articles on the Objectors to the [3mMeditations [0medited by Roger Ariew and Marjorie Grene 
(Chicago: University of Chicago Press, 1995) includes contributions from leading French Descartes scholars. 

[1mุงููุธุฑูุฉ ุงูุฃุฎูุงููุฉ ููุชุงุจุงุช ุฏููุงุฑุช ูู ุงูุทุจ [0m

Texts, including letters, relevant to a study of what Descartes calls โmoralsโ, are assembled in John Blom (trans.), [3mDescartes: 
His Moral Philosophy and Psychology [0m(Hassocks: Harvester, 1978). 

Descartesโs medical writings are discussed and interpreted in Richard Carter, [3mDescartesโs Medical Philosophy [0m(Baltimore: Johns 
Hopkins University Press, 1978).

On Cartesianism in philosophy after Descartesโs death, see Norman Kemp Smith, [3mStudies in the Cartesian Philosophy [0m(London:

For an indication of reactions against Descartes in latter-day philosophy, see Rรฉe (cited above), and Richard Rorty, [3mPhilosophy 
and the Mirror of Nature [0m(Oxford: Blackwell, 1980).
